## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (dependent on position x), possible damping (dependent on velocity v), and possible time-dependent driving forces.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external driving)
- Pendulum-like oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v**3 (combined nonlinearities)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2)**(-1) (rational restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power position terms (x, x**3, x**5) indicate symmetric restoring potentials; even powers (x**2) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Position-velocity coupling terms like x**2 * v suggest amplitude-dependent damping (Van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicate periodic external driving forces
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) indicate periodic potentials or pendulum-like dynamics
- The sign of the cubic term relative to the linear term distinguishes hardening (same sign as linear) vs softening (opposite sign) springs
- Absence of explicit time dependence indicates an autonomous/conservative or autonomously damped system
- Rational functions of x like x/(1+c*x**2) can represent bounded restoring forces that saturate at large displacements
- Products of v with even powers of x (e.g., x**2 * v) create limit cycle behavior through amplitude-dependent energy balance

Can `x*exp(-|x|)` be represented by `x*|x|^c`? No - `x*|x|^c = |x|^c * x = sign(x)*|x|^(c+1)`, while `x*exp(-|x|)` has exponential decay.
